<span id="freeTextContainer12599099250594095020">Ace reporter John Cotton is a fly on the wall -- seeing all, hearing all, and keeping out of sight. But the game changes when he finds his best friend's corpse sprawled on the marble floor of the central rotunda of the U.S. Capitol. Suddenly Cotton knows too much about a scandal centered around a senatorial candidate, a million-dollar scam, and a murder. And he hears the p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12599099250594095020">Ace reporter John Cotton is a fly on the wall -- seeing all, hearing all, and keeping out of sight. But the game changes when he finds his best friend's corpse sprawled on the marble floor of the central rotunda of the U.S. Capitol. Suddenly Cotton knows too much about a scandal centered around a senatorial candidate, a million-dollar scam, and a murder. And he hears the pursuing footsteps of powerful people who have something to hide ... and a willingness to kill to keep their secrets hidden.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794461063" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/695116-jim" class="left imgcol" title="Jim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" alt="Jim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/794461063?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 22, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/695116-jim" class="user" title="Jim">Jim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17446537-the-fly-on-the-wall" title="Audio 9780062284792" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction" class="actionLinkLite">2fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=mystery-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer794461063">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2964912412630165260">My father-in-law was a fan of Hillerman's. When he died over a decade ago, I read several of the books he had &amp; remembered liking them, but not being wowed. I have to say that this one surprised me. Hillerman handled some very tough themes about reporting, truth, &amp; integrity. Right &amp; wrong blurred the deeper the reporter dug &amp; the ending was full of wonderful surprises. There was a realistic quality throughout, too. The hero isn't particularly brave, smart, nor perfect in any way</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2964912412630165260">My father-in-law was a fan of Hillerman's. When he died over a decade ago, I read several of the books he had &amp; remembered liking them, but not being wowed. I have to say that this one surprised me. Hillerman handled some very tough themes about reporting, truth, &amp; integrity. Right &amp; wrong blurred the deeper the reporter dug &amp; the ending was full of wonderful surprises. There was a realistic quality throughout, too. The hero isn't particularly brave, smart, nor perfect in any way. He's a good man that does his best under some trying circumstances &amp; does pretty well, though.<br /><br />The reading was well done, too. I'm definitely going to look for more by this author in this format.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_829285995">

  <a href="/user/show/350218-booklady" class="left imgcol" title="booklady"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1354374319p2/350218.jpg" alt="booklady" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/829285995?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 22, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/350218-booklady" class="user" title="booklady">booklady</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15746258-the-fly-on-the-wall" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/350218-booklady?shelf=political" class="actionLinkLite">political</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer829285995">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16191818464222272692">I was introduced to native Oklahoman Tony Hillerman, author of <em>The Fly on the Wall</em>, by one of my favorite senior citizens, a 93 years young Okie-born lady. As a transplant myself, it’s good to pick up a bit of the local flavor. <em>The Fly on the Wall</em> was written in 1971, so as a political-mystery-thriller, it’s a bit dated. The main character, a reporter investigating a friend and colleague’s suspicious death was renting a typewriter of all things. I can barely remember using one. Plot moves quickl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16191818464222272692">I was introduced to native Oklahoman Tony Hillerman, author of <em>The Fly on the Wall</em>, by one of my favorite senior citizens, a 93 years young Okie-born lady. As a transplant myself, it’s good to pick up a bit of the local flavor. <em>The Fly on the Wall</em> was written in 1971, so as a political-mystery-thriller, it’s a bit dated. The main character, a reporter investigating a friend and colleague’s suspicious death was renting a typewriter of all things. I can barely remember using one. Plot moves quickly, but doesn't have so many things going on at the same time, you need a notepad by your side to keep track of them all. This book's not for everybody, but I found it interesting for perspective’s sake and also as a change-up read. Plan to sample more by Hillerman; my friend has a big stack by him. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16191818464222272692">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_729152317">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729152317" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7607058-susan-oleksiw" class="left imgcol" title="Susan Oleksiw"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442465930p2/7607058.jpg" alt="Susan Oleksiw" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/729152317?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 27, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7607058-susan-oleksiw" class="user" title="Susan Oleksiw">Susan Oleksiw</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer729152317">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11104510480933491158">This mystery is the second one published by Hillerman, after his first mystery set in Navajo country, The Blessing Way.<br /><br />In the Fly on the Wall, John Cotton is a statehouse reporter and has just filed his story when a colleague comes into the pressroom. Merrill McDaniels, known as Mac, comes into file his story, but he’s a little drunk and Cotton offers to file something for him and tell his editor he went home sick. Cotton tries to get him on home but Mac says he’s celebrating breaking the story</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11104510480933491158">This mystery is the second one published by Hillerman, after his first mystery set in Navajo country, The Blessing Way.<br /><br />In the Fly on the Wall, John Cotton is a statehouse reporter and has just filed his story when a colleague comes into the pressroom. Merrill McDaniels, known as Mac, comes into file his story, but he’s a little drunk and Cotton offers to file something for him and tell his editor he went home sick. Cotton tries to get him on home but Mac says he’s celebrating breaking the story of a lifetime. Cotton doesn’t really believe him, but Mac heads on home. A few minutes later a man enters and rummages through Mac’s desk looking for his notebook, telling Cotton that Mac forgot it and sent his friend for it. A few minutes later Mac is found dead.<br /><br />So begins Cotton’s at first desultory investigation into the big story Mac was working on. He finds Mac’s notebook, traces back the other man’s investigation, and wonders what Mac could have been excited about. When another reporter is killed driving Cotton’s car, Cotton at first thinks only it was an accident. He keeps digging, looking for the story while the other reporters are covering Governor Roark’s political future, Senator Clark’s plans, and small struggles over legislation. Then Cotton begins to have enough pieces to put together into a small puzzle, and he gets another warning, this one unmistakable in its meaning.<br /><br />This is a masterfully plotted and steadily paced mystery that brings forward all the details of a major scam, how the players hide themselves and their cronies, and how easy it is to fool the tax payer, the reporters, and other politicians. Hillerman offers one surprise after another, and even the last two pages brings a stunning reversal. Hillerman was a journalist for many years, and his skill and experience show on every page. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11104510480933491158">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/1467051881?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4228172-helen" class="user" title="Helen">Helen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1022473.The_Fly_On_The_Wall" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380441563" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1467051881">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8429664835663482194">Dated but still engrossing--once you get past all the technical and political detail. The hook works, but the story slows in the first half when Cotton is doing his investigative journalism digging for facts and when he explains how the state capitol political pecking order works. This is important detail, but it slows the pace. That pace picks up greatly once Cotton becomes the target of very dangerous people.<br /><br />Even though this is dated (technologically), the topic is surprisingly timely, conside</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8429664835663482194">Dated but still engrossing--once you get past all the technical and political detail. The hook works, but the story slows in the first half when Cotton is doing his investigative journalism digging for facts and when he explains how the state capitol political pecking order works. This is important detail, but it slows the pace. That pace picks up greatly once Cotton becomes the target of very dangerous people.<br /><br />Even though this is dated (technologically), the topic is surprisingly timely, considering all the money in state and national politics. As a newsman, Cotton wrestles with very real ethical and moral questions that never go out of date.<br /><br />I was closer to a 3.5 than a 3 rating because of the theme and Hillerman's trademark gift for writing suspense, which shines in the second half. I'm glad I picked this up.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8429664835663482194">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_974050360">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/974050360" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/674575-john" class="left imgcol" title="John"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1325044654p2/674575.jpg" alt="John" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/974050360?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 18, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/674575-john" class="user" title="John">John</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/674575-john?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer974050360">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5541629652443945592">I have put off reading The Fly on the Wall for a long while, since it’s the only mystery Hillerman wrote that is not about his great detectives Joe Leaphorn and Jim Chee. Frankly, however, I’m running out of Hillerman’s Navajo novels to read, and so I picked this one up when I thought I might need some light reading on a weekend trip. As it turns out, The Fly on the Wall is one of Hillerman’s strongest efforts, and I thoroughly enjoyed it.<br /><br />The novel follows John Cotton, a political reporter at th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5541629652443945592">I have put off reading The Fly on the Wall for a long while, since it’s the only mystery Hillerman wrote that is not about his great detectives Joe Leaphorn and Jim Chee. Frankly, however, I’m running out of Hillerman’s Navajo novels to read, and so I picked this one up when I thought I might need some light reading on a weekend trip. As it turns out, The Fly on the Wall is one of Hillerman’s strongest efforts, and I thoroughly enjoyed it.<br /><br />The novel follows John Cotton, a political reporter at the Kansas state capitol. One evening, a drunk fellow reporter gives him a tip that he’ll soon be sharing some information with him on a huge story. The reporter, of course, ends up dead by the morning, but none of Cotton’s inquiries turn up scandal of the level which the reporter had hinted at. Before long, though, Cotton seems to be making someone mad, and he starts trying to put together the odd shaped pieces of the puzzle.<br /><br />I found Cotton to be an intriguing character, and the book was well-plotted and fast paced. I also especially enjoyed the unique setting of this one. I’ve always enjoyed just how much you can learn from reading Hillerman’s novels set in the Four Corners, and the midwestern state government setting was itself educational, albeit in a different way. Even though The Fly on the Wall is not a part of Hillerman’s famous and excellent Navajo series, it is still written by Tony Hillerman and is thus a fantastically entertaining read for his fans.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5541629652443945592">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_888972977">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/888972977" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/29894186-david" class="left imgcol" title="David"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395871331p2/29894186.jpg" alt="David" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/888972977?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 26, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/29894186-david" class="user" title="David">David</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6620395-the-fly-on-the-wall" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer888972977">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8638528531254991358">Tony Hillerman's "The Fly on the Wall" is not one of his "Leaphorn &amp; Chee" novels. It's a mystery set in nameless non-Western state capital. Unfortunately, it's not a very good book. First of all, the story is all about politics. That's a big turn-off for me, but for others, it might be fine. Next, the protagonist doesn't seem to have enough neurons to rub against each other to create a spark. Much of the plot consists of him entirely ignoring blatantly obvious signals that something's going</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8638528531254991358">Tony Hillerman's "The Fly on the Wall" is not one of his "Leaphorn &amp; Chee" novels. It's a mystery set in nameless non-Western state capital. Unfortunately, it's not a very good book. First of all, the story is all about politics. That's a big turn-off for me, but for others, it might be fine. Next, the protagonist doesn't seem to have enough neurons to rub against each other to create a spark. Much of the plot consists of him entirely ignoring blatantly obvious signals that something's going on, talking to people he shouldn't, and not talking to people he should. Now, even with that, the plot is a bit interesting. So, I might have been able to give the book a neutral rating if those were the only things I had problems with. But, the ending of the book is so bad that I had to drop it another star. Unless I'm misinterpreting Hillerman's ending, it seems like he's saying that politics excuses corruption and murder. Perhaps he's being facetious or ironic and I'm missing it. But, with how the protagonist acts at the end, I can only rate the book at a Not Very Good 2 stars out of 5.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8638528531254991358">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/1196786-mary" class="user" title="Mary">Mary</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer74808936">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14436713968941893822">This is not one of the Navajo novels...it is a political story with lots of the 'dirty politics' that make my head spin. The protagonist is a newspaper reporter on the 'capitol beat' in his state; he gets involved after the suspicious death (attributed to suicide) of a co-worker. Someone is looking for the dead man's reporter's notebook. Why? Even with the notebook, there are many questions to be answered. I found the story to be a little long and drawn out, and the details of the corruption wer</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14436713968941893822">This is not one of the Navajo novels...it is a political story with lots of the 'dirty politics' that make my head spin. The protagonist is a newspaper reporter on the 'capitol beat' in his state; he gets involved after the suspicious death (attributed to suicide) of a co-worker. Someone is looking for the dead man's reporter's notebook. Why? Even with the notebook, there are many questions to be answered. I found the story to be a little long and drawn out, and the details of the corruption were hard for me to keep track of (and by today's standards, they seemed very minor!). I much prefer Hillerman's other mysteries, but he was obviously well-versed in the underbelly of the political process.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2152464248402495319">Boy, I was really getting into this investigative journalist/crime solver mystery until the end. I didn't get that part. This involves politics in Washington DC (I think?) and the governors of New Mexico (I think) and some other governors and political type people and some lawyers and some contractors and some newspaper people. The journalist part of developed well - the writer going around, uncovering information of fraud and deceit and then finding out who the bad guys are, all the while being</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2152464248402495319">Boy, I was really getting into this investigative journalist/crime solver mystery until the end. I didn't get that part. This involves politics in Washington DC (I think?) and the governors of New Mexico (I think) and some other governors and political type people and some lawyers and some contractors and some newspaper people. The journalist part of developed well - the writer going around, uncovering information of fraud and deceit and then finding out who the bad guys are, all the while being a target himself. As far as a crime/mystery story, this really is a 3 but I gave it a 4 for the journalist slant.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6698538959370048404">When I see a book I haven’t yet read by Tony Hillerman I quickly snatch it up, because I love his Navajo stories, so was surprised to find that ‘The Fly on The Wall’ was vastly different from the others as it deliberately focuses on an ace reporter and a dead colleague’s notebook in an unknown capitol city. It then dawned on me that this story was one of Mr. Hillerman’s early works, and at one time, he was a reporter, so all was made clear. The story was sufficiently interesting throughout, though it did not quite live up to my anticipation of a captivating read.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1046839232">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11566365-ed?shelf=reporter" class="actionLinkLite">reporter</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11566365-ed?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1046839232">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11376326978533475340">A non-series novel from Tony Hillerman, Southwest author best known for his Joe Leaphorn and Jim Chee, Navajo policemen series. Although Hillerman is identified with the American Southwest, this political thriller takes place in a snowy, unnamed, Midwestern state capitol. Political corruption and murder have the ability to fuel an absorbing story but this one, while entertaining, misses being riveting. My opinion is not universal, the book was a Finalist 1972 Edgar Award for Best Mystery; and, n</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11376326978533475340">A non-series novel from Tony Hillerman, Southwest author best known for his Joe Leaphorn and Jim Chee, Navajo policemen series. Although Hillerman is identified with the American Southwest, this political thriller takes place in a snowy, unnamed, Midwestern state capitol. Political corruption and murder have the ability to fuel an absorbing story but this one, while entertaining, misses being riveting. My opinion is not universal, the book was a Finalist 1972 Edgar Award for Best Mystery; and, named to Ninety Classics of Crime Fiction 1900-1975, ed. Jacques Barzun and Wendell Hertig Taylor.<br /><br />Non-series - Ace reporter John Cotton is a fly on the wall -- seeing all, hearing all, and keeping out of sight. But the game changes when he finds a fellow reporter's corpse sprawled on the marble floor of the central rotunda of the State Capitol. The shocking pages of the dead reporter's notebook tell of a scandal involving a senatorial candidate, a million-dollar scam, and a murder. And he hears the pursuing footsteps of powerful people who have something to hide ... and a willingness to kill to keep their secrets hidden.<br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_917328127">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/917328127" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8471272-lillian-carl" class="left imgcol" title="Lillian Carl"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442453591p2/8471272.jpg" alt="Lillian Carl" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/917328127?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8471272-lillian-carl" class="user" title="Lillian Carl">Lillian Carl</a>

          added it




        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer917328127">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4784053731320578985">I picked up this novel expecting it to be the second of Hillerman's Chee and Leaphorn Navajo mysteries. It isn't. I'm guessing (but it's only a guess) he wrote this book while waiting to see if The Blessing Way, the first Navajo book, was successful enough to justify his going on with the series.<br /><br />This story centers around John Cotton, a political reporter at an unidentified midwestern state capitol. A colleague of his is murdered soon after uncovering a scandal and Cotton follows up.<br /><br />While Cotton</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4784053731320578985">I picked up this novel expecting it to be the second of Hillerman's Chee and Leaphorn Navajo mysteries. It isn't. I'm guessing (but it's only a guess) he wrote this book while waiting to see if The Blessing Way, the first Navajo book, was successful enough to justify his going on with the series.<br /><br />This story centers around John Cotton, a political reporter at an unidentified midwestern state capitol. A colleague of his is murdered soon after uncovering a scandal and Cotton follows up.<br /><br />While Cotton is a nicely done character, I sorely missed Chee and Leaphorn and the southwestern settings (which appear only briefly). Published in 1971, the story is an intersting time capsule on how reporters worked before the digital age, with Cotton working on a typewriter, using a teletype, etc. And depending on the day's newspaper publication schedule.<br /><br />It also shows how political cynicism is nothing at all new.<br /><br />Beyond some nice action sequenes, though, much of the book is the deadly dull exposition of how Cotton works out the scandal, which doesn't even involve, say, interns in blue dresses but highway-building. Yawn.<br /><br />The ending was supposed to be shocking, I suppose, except I've seen two almost identical patterns played out in TV shows in just the last couple of months, so I'm afraid I greeted the denouement with yet another moderately cynical yawn.<br /><br />Not a bad book, but not one I really enjoyed, either. I spent most of the time skimming the pages. However, I have Hillerman's A Thief of Time sitting on my coffee table and am anticipating that.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4784053731320578985">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38484010">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7712267667720878531">Picked this up for a quarter at the library--read it on the bus in only three trips. It's an early Hillerman and not a Jim Chee story. I enjoyed the robustness of this example of Hillerman's writing as a younger man (his later books are entertaining but often don't feel as taut and energetic as this one did). Also liked the fact that the ending was less predictable than I'd anticipated. Definitely a good chilling-out book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5877880-jamie-barringer-ravenmount?shelf=f-mysteries-and-crime" class="actionLinkLite">f-mysteries-and-crime</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1200949563">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15947766107719627008">This was a fun, fast read. It might be a bit dry for readers who are not interested in political thrillers and state-level politics, but it is well thought out and well paced. Mr. Cotton is a bit more naive than I would have expected, given his resume, but had he been quicker to figure out that his life was in danger, the story might have been quite a bit different. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1364253683">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8633779573591437323">Well....<br /><br />The book is slow paced and takes forever to get to the action. The narrative is standard Hillerman laconic, but it lacks the charm of the Jim Chee books. Joe Cotton is so disconnected from the action that he never really connects with the reader either, not even when he's being tracked like a deer or having a gun held on him.<br /><br />I, personally, had issue with the lack of detailed location. Other than one scene taking place in New Mexico, the rest of the book is in an unnamed city somewhere in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8633779573591437323">Well....<br /><br />The book is slow paced and takes forever to get to the action. The narrative is standard Hillerman laconic, but it lacks the charm of the Jim Chee books. Joe Cotton is so disconnected from the action that he never really connects with the reader either, not even when he's being tracked like a deer or having a gun held on him.<br /><br />I, personally, had issue with the lack of detailed location. Other than one scene taking place in New Mexico, the rest of the book is in an unnamed city somewhere in the US. It made it ard to get a grasp on the scenery, the people and for a book about politics, the politics and what made the politicians tick.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3644721261475727783">Interested in Hillerman's Navajo series, I picked up this book to read. For fans of Hillerman, I should note that this book actually is not actually a part of the Navajo series. The Fly on the Wall involves corruption and politics and the reporter John Cotton who tries to uncover it. I prefer the Navajo series, but this was still an enjoyable read with plenty of suspense. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/1374822-myra" class="user" title="Myra">Myra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer148776768">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12602804955629942469">This was a different Tony Hillerman for me. I'm a fan of his Navajo books, but this was about a newspaperman investigating corruption in state government and had nothing to do with Native Americans except for one chapter being set in New Mexico near Santa Fe. The rest of the story is set in an anonymous Midwestern city. It was an easy enough read. Hillerman's books always are. But the story didn't really capture my imagination like his Native American stories do. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");

      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26917.Tony_Hillerman">About Tony Hillerman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/26917.Tony_Hillerman"><img alt="26917" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1281729229p2/26917.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer10225632313328189866">Tony Hillerman, who was born in Sacred Heart, Oklahoma, was a decorated combat veteran from World War II, serving as a mortarman in the 103rd Infantry Division and earning the Silver Star, the Bronze Star, and a Purple Heart. Later, he worked as a journalist from 1948 to 1962. Then he earned a Masters degree and taught journalism from 1966 to 1987 at the University of New Mexico in Albuquerque, wh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10225632313328189866">Tony Hillerman, who was born in Sacred Heart, Oklahoma, was a decorated combat veteran from World War II, serving as a mortarman in the 103rd Infantry Division and earning the Silver Star, the Bronze Star, and a Purple Heart. Later, he worked as a journalist from 1948 to 1962. Then he earned a Masters degree and taught journalism from 1966 to 1987 at the University of New Mexico in Albuquerque, where he resided with his wife until his death in 2008. Hillerman, a consistently bestselling author, was ranked as New Mexico's 25th wealthiest man in 1996. - Wikipedia</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10225632313328189866">...more</a>
